Character 1: [approaching footsteps] That's a hell of a blowout you got there—मैं 20 साल से tires बना रही हूँ लेकिन steel belts को इस तरह फटते कभी नहीं देखा।
1. [tersely] Yeah, well, I was doing seventy on a straight highway, और वो भी बिल्कुल नई Michelins के साथ, तो मुझे खुद समझ नहीं आ रहा क्या हुआ है।
Character 1: Mind if I take a closer look? [kneeling down] Sidewall पर ये scoring patterns देखो, ये इतने uniform हैं कि normal road debris से नहीं हो सकते।
2. [impatiently] Look, I appreciate you stopping, लेकिन मैंने पहले ही roadside assistance को बुला लिया है और वो एक घंटे में आ जाएंगे।
Character 1: [focused] Someone cut through your tire valve stem with precision tools—यहाँ ये निशान देख रही हो? ये कोई accident नहीं था, ये तो highway speed पर fail करने के लिए specifically design किया गया था।
3. [voice dropping] What makes you so sure about that? [pause] ज़्यादातर लोग तो ऐसी चीज़ें notice भी नहीं करते या फिर उन्हें पता ही नहीं होता क्या देखना है।
Character 1: I build tires for military contractors, तो मैं sabotage को पहचान सकती हूँ, और जिसने भी ये किया है उसे exactly पता था कि maximum damage के लिए कहाँ cuts लगाने हैं। [standing up slowly]
4. Military contractors. [bitter laugh] वाह, कमाल है। और मैं सोच रही थी कि आज मेरी सबसे बड़ी problem अपने clients को ये explain करना होगा कि हमारा algorithm उस semiconductor shortage को कैसे miss कर गया।
Character 1: [sharply] Semiconductor shortage? तुम्हारा algorithm—रुको, तुम कोई ordinary banker तो नहीं हो ना? तुम defense industry supply chains के साथ काम करती हो?
5. [carefully measured] I manage predictive models for commodity futures, जिसमें rubber और synthetic materials भी आते हैं, जो कभी-कभी certain government interests के साथ overlap कर सकते हैं, हाँ।
# --- SIMPLE_TAGS ---
Character 1: [firmly] देखिये, मुझे एकदम साफ़-साफ़ जानना है कि आपके टेंट कैसे बनते हैं, कौन से materials use करती हैं आप, क्योंकि 300 refugees chemical burns और सांस की तकलीफ़ से जूझ रहे हैं... उस spill site के पास आपके टेंट में रहने के बाद।
6. [defensive] मेरे टेंट तो बस canvas और रस्सी के हैं, ऐसा कुछ नहीं जिससे ये symptoms हो सकें। [frustrated] अरे मैं 15 साल से ये shelters बना रही हूँ, पूरी दुनिया के disaster zones में भेजती हूँ, और एक बार भी... एक बार भी किसी को materials से कोई बीमारी नहीं हुई।
Character 1: [passionately] इसीलिए तो मैं यहाँ हूँ—आपके टेंट ने ये नहीं किया, उन्होंने तो बस reveal किया है। [pause] Chemical company कह रही है कि refugees को exposure कहीं और से हुआ था, लेकिन आपके canvas ने contaminated groundwater के toxins को absorb करके concentrate कर दिया।
7. [quietly] तो मेरे shelters जो... जिनसे बचाना था उन्हें, वो actually [exhales] ज़हर के साथ फंसा दिया? [bitter] हे भगवान, मैं तो एक-एक टांका ये सोचकर लगाती हूँ कि किसी परिवार को इसमें सुरक्षा मिलेगी।
Character 1: [empathetically] सुनिये, आपके टेंट नहीं होते तो वो लोग 48 घंटे में exposure से मर जाते। [stern] अब हमें आपकी expertise चाहिए ये prove करने के लिए कि chemicals ने canvas fibers में इतनी concentration में penetrate किया जो हर safety standard की धज्जियाँ उड़ा देता है।
8. [curious] आप चाहती हैं मैं chemical company के खिलाफ़ गवाही दूं? [nervous] मैं तो बस एक कारीगर हूँ जो अकेले अपनी workshop में काम करती है, corporate lawyers से भिड़ने वाली नहीं हूँ।
Character 1: [reassuring] आप अकेली नहीं होंगी—मेरे पास 17 environmental scientists हैं और 4 और manufacturers जो आपकी testimony support करने को तैयार हैं। [confidently] जो मेरे पास नहीं है वो है कोई ऐसा जो tent construction इतना समझता हो कि jury को absorption rates समझा सके।
9. [hesitantly] बात ये है कि canvas की breathability ही अच्छे shelter की पहचान है—हवा का flow मतलब mold और condensation नहीं होगा। [sighs] लेकिन वही porosity का मतलब है कि airborne chemicals कुछ ही घंटों में fibers को saturate कर सकते हैं।
Character 1: बिलकुल, और company को पता था कि उनकी storage facility camp से upwind थी। [angry] उनके पास meteorological data था जो बताता था कि हवा का रुख़ contaminated vapor को सीधे refugee settlement में हर रात ले जाएगा।
10. [shocked] पता था उन्हें? [very quietly] बच्चे सो रहे थे उन टेंटों में, pregnant औरतें, बूढ़े लोग जो पहले ही सब कुछ खो चुके थे, और company को पता था कि वो ज़हर सांस ले रहे हैं?
# --- CUSTOMER_SUPPORT ---
Customer: *exhales* मैं अभी किसी से बात कर रही थी और हम—नहीं मेरा मतलब, कॉल कट गई।
11. अरे नहीं। अरे मुझे—मुझे बहुत अफ़सोस है। ये तो। बहुत frustrating होगा। मैं आपका account खोलती हूं—आपका फोन नंबर क्या है last में?
Customer: 4782 है। उन्होंने कहा था manager से बात कराएंगे पर फिर कुछ नहीं हुआ।
12. अच्छा। 4782। मिल गया। देख रही हूं... ठीक है आपका case number CSE-9441-DX यहाँ है। दिख रहा है disconnected हुआ। 2:47pm पे। मुझे सच में—genuinely अफ़सोस है ये हुआ।
Customer: मेरी बेटी की दवाई deny हो गई और मुझे बस—मुझे सच में आज ही ये solve करना है।
13. ओह। दवाई। ये तो—मेरा मतलब ये तो serious है। बहुत serious। मैं अभी। आपको management से connect करती हूं तुरंत। Denial का reference number MED-7823-PQ है। एक minute।
Customer: क्या मैं कुछ गलत कर रही हूं? मैं बार-बार call करती हूं और कहीं नहीं पहुंचती।
14. नहीं नहीं नहीं। बिल्कुल नहीं। आप—ये आपकी गलती नहीं है। System में दिख रहा है। आज तीन calls। Account 8827-MED-43। ये तो। हमारी तरफ से है। पूरी तरह।
Customer: *sharp inhale* वो कह रहे हैं कल तक चाहिए वरना फिर से शुरू करना पड़ेगा।
15. कल तक। अच्छा। Urgent है फिर। खोल रही हूं। Manager queue का—sorry, मेरा मतलब supervisor tier। Badge S-5543। Average wait है। अम्म। बारह minute अभी।
# --- MONOLOGUE ---
16. [very quietly] पता है, जब Oscars में मेरा नाम पुकारा गया, मुझे कुछ सुनाई ही नहीं दे रहा था। Ironic है ना? Sound mixer जो खुद कुछ सुन नहीं पा रही। [chuckle] लेकिन वो दिन रेगिस्तान में—अरे यार, वो दिन। हम एक बेहद नाज़ुक dialogue scene capture करने की कोशिश कर रहे थे, और हवा बस रुकने का नाम ही नहीं ले रही थी। [frustrated] चार घंटे हम इंतज़ार करते रहे। पूरे चार घंटे। Actors का दिमाग खराब हो रहा था, director इधर-उधर चक्कर काट रहे थे, और मैं बस वहाँ अपने headphones लगाए बैठी थी, सुन रही थी बस, अम्म... बस शोर ही शोर। [pause] और फिर अचानक—खामोशी। जैसे रेगिस्तान ने अपनी सांस रोक ली हो। [very excited] मैंने signal दिया और हमने roll किया, और perfect था यार! हर फुसफुसाहट, हर सांस, कपड़ों की सरसराहट—सब कुछ एकदम साफ़। [slowly] वही take है जो film में सुनाई देता है। जिसने सबको रुला दिया था। [short pause] लोग हमेशा पूछते हैं उन बड़े explosion scenes के बारे में या action sequences के बारे में, लेकिन बात वो नहीं है। ये छोटे, शांत पल हैं जो, अ... जो सच में मायने रखते हैं। वो पल जहाँ आप किसी की आवाज़ में उसका दिल टूटते सुन सकते हैं। [passionately] यही तो हमने उस दिन रेगिस्तान में capture किया था। [smiling speaking] और अब मेरे shelf पे एक golden statue रखी है जो कहती है कि हमने कुछ तो सही किया।
# --- GENERAL_TAGS ---
Character 1: Rubber futures. [exhales] अच्छा, अब tire की बात समझ आई।
17. [suddenly alert] What do you mean 'that explains the tire'? क्या तुम्हें पता है कि मेरी गाड़ी के साथ ये किसने किया होगा?
Character 1: Three weeks ago, someone tried to breach our facility's database, वो classified tire specifications ढूंढ रहे थे—वो specifications जो अगर leak हो जाएं तो global rubber prices affect हो सकते हैं। [grimly] लगता है उन्होंने message भेजने का दूसरा तरीका ढूंढ लिया।
18. [voice tightening] A message about what exactly? मैं सिर्फ algorithms चलाती हूँ, मैं दुश्मन नहीं बनाती, कम से कम ऐसे नहीं जो tires काटते फिरें।
Character 1: Your algorithm probably flagged something it shouldn't have, शायद कोई shell company जो Malaysia के through synthetic rubber move कर रही हो? [watching closely] ये लोग notice होना पसंद नहीं करते।
19. [defensive] Even if that were true, which I'm not confirming, तुम्हें Malaysian shell companies के बारे में कैसे पता होगा जबकि तुम Ohio में tires बनाती हो?
Character 1: [quietly] Because I don't just build tires, मैं track करती हूँ कि हमारे materials कहाँ से आते हैं, और हाल में, [sighs], कोई dummy corporations के through shipments reroute कर रहा है।
20. So we're both watching the same supply chain from different angles. [hollow laugh] कोई wonder नहीं कि कोई चाहता है कि हम देखना बंद कर दें।
Character 1: [firmly] You need to get off this highway right now—अगर उन्होंने तुम्हारा tire sabotage किया है, तो तुम्हारी roadside assistance call भी पक्का compromise है।
21. [resigned] Get in my truck then, कहीं और जाकर figure out करेंगे जहाँ हम empty highway asphalt पर sitting target नहीं हों। [keys jingling] अपना phone गाड़ी में ही छोड़ दो।

# --- GENERAL_TAGS (continued) ---
Character 1: [hushed panic] You can't be here—the bailiff said no contact between witnesses and defendants, and if they catch us talking in this stairwell, they'll throw out the whole case.
22. [desperate whisper] I know what the rules say, but you're the only one who saw what really happened that night at the warehouse, and my lawyer says without you, I'm looking at fifteen to twenty years.
Character 1: I already told the prosecutor I wouldn't testify, that I didn't see anything clear enough to matter, and honestly, [exhales], getting involved in this mess could destroy everything I've built.
23. Please, just listen—
Character 1: [voice breaking] My kids, my job at the hospital, everything depends on me staying out of this, and you know what happens to people who testify in cases like yours.
24. [defeated tone] You think I wanted this? You think I wanted to drag you into my nightmare? But that security footage is grainy, and without your testimony confirming I was defending myself, the jury will believe their narrative.
Character 1: Defending yourself? Marcus, you broke that man's jaw in three places, and even if he came at you first, [swallows hard], the prosecution has painted you as the aggressor.
25. [urgently whispered] Because they don't know about his knife, the one you saw him pull before I ever touched him—the one that conveniently disappeared before the cops arrived.
Character 1: Even if I testified about the knife, they'd tear me apart on cross-examination, bring up my old arrests, make me look like just another unreliable witness from the neighborhood.
26. [hollow whisper] So that's it.
Character 1: Your lawyer has other witnesses, other angles to work, and maybe the forensics will show something, maybe they'll find DNA evidence or, [sighs], I don't know, something that doesn't require me.
27. [bitterly quiet] The other witnesses were all inside when it started, and forensics can't find evidence of a knife that someone made disappear—you know that as well as I do.
Character 1: [trembling] If I testify and they connect me to you, to your past, my ex will use it to take my kids away—she's already looking for any excuse.
28. I have kids too. [pause]
Character 1: [quietly anguished] Don't do that, don't put that on me, because I've been carrying this guilt for weeks already, knowing what I know and staying silent.
29. Then you do know it's wrong, keeping quiet when you could save an innocent man—when you could tell them the truth about what really happened out there. [voice cracking]
Character 1: [barely audible] Innocent.
30. [desperately] In this case, yes, I'm innocent of what they're charging me with, and you know that because you were there, you saw him come at me with that blade.
Character 1: [resigned whisper] The recess is almost over, and if we're seen together, it won't matter what either of us says because they'll throw everything out on procedural grounds.
31. [final plea] Just think about it, please—think about what you'd want if it was you sitting in that defendant's chair, knowing someone could save you but chose not to.
Character 1: [defensive] Look, I don't know what you think you saw on that video, but lifting a single chair to move it out of the way isn't the same as, um, eight hours of heavy machinery work.
32. [skeptically] Mr. Peterson, the surveillance shows you carrying a couch down your front steps, then loading it into a pickup truck without any apparent difficulty or, uh, signs of the debilitating pain you described in your claim.
Character 1: [frustrated] That was my neighbor's couch, okay? And I was helping for maybe, what, five minutes total? [sighs] My back was screaming the entire time but I couldn't just leave them stranded.
33. Mm-hmm. And the footage from three days later showing you, err, playing basketball at the park? Was your back screaming then too, or was that a different neighbor needing help?
Character 1: [incredulous] Basketball? I was shooting free throws with my kid for ten minutes, not running full court! Jesus, do you people just follow me around all day waiting for me to, I dunno, bend wrong or something?
34. We conduct routine investigations on claims exceeding fifty thousand dollars, Mr. Peterson, and frankly, your activities don't align with someone who claims they can't sit, stand, or walk for more than, umm, fifteen minutes at a time.
Character 1: You don't understand—
35. [firmly] I understand perfectly well that you filed for permanent disability while maintaining a remarkably active lifestyle, and that's, honestly, that's a serious problem we need to address.
Character 1: Active lifestyle? Are you kidding me? I take enough painkillers to knock out a horse just to get through breakfast! [voice cracking] Some days I can move around okay, others I'm flat on my back crying.
36. [unmoved] Yet you never mentioned these 'good days' in any of your medical evaluations or depositions, did you? Every single report describes constant, unrelenting pain that prevents any physical activity whatsoever.
Character 1: Because that's what the doctors told me to focus on—the worst of it! They said if I mentioned the occasional decent day, you people would use it against me, and look, [bitter laugh], here we are.
37. [coolly] So you're admitting to deliberately misrepresenting your condition? Because that's, uh, that's actually insurance fraud, Mr. Peterson, which carries criminal penalties including potential jail time.
Character 1: Misrepresenting? No, I—look, I got hurt at work, really hurt, and some days are better than others but I still can't do my job anymore, alright? Isn't that what matters here?
38. What matters is the truth, and right now I'm seeing significant discrepancies between your statements and your actions that, frankly, could result in immediate termination of benefits and, umm, possible prosecution.
Character 1: [desperately] Please, I've got three kids and a mortgage, okay? I'm not faking anything—my back is destroyed, I just, sometimes I push through the pain when I have to because life doesn't stop, you know?
39. [slightly softer] Mr. Peterson, I'm going to recommend a full medical reevaluation with an independent physician, and I strongly suggest you be, err, completely honest about your condition this time, including these variable pain levels you're describing.
Character 1: [defeated] Fine, whatever you need. But when your doctor confirms what I've been saying all along—that I'm permanently damaged goods—I want an apology for this, this witch hunt you're putting me through.
40. [returning to professional tone] We'll see what the evaluation reveals, won't we? In the meantime, your benefits are suspended pending review. [pause] You'll receive official notification within seventy-two hours.
Character 1: [quietly furious] Suspended? My kids need to eat while you play detective! This is exactly why people hate insurance companies—you collect premiums for years then look for any excuse not to pay when we actually need help.
41. [standing to leave] The review process typically takes four to six weeks, Mr. Peterson, and I'd advise you to consult with an attorney if you haven't already. [flatly] Have a good day.
Character 1: मैं बार-बार launch event को अपने दिमाग में replay कर रही हूँ, लोगों के चेहरे देख रही हूँ जब उन्होंने पहली बार product try किया था—वो अजीब सी confusion, पता है ना? 3 साल की development और किसी को समझ ही नहीं आया कि हम कौन सा problem solve कर रहे थे।
42. [gently] Product development की सबसे कड़वी सच्चाई ये है कि बिना empathy के innovation बस एक महंगा अंदाज़ा है, और trust me, मैंने सालों में ऐसी सैकड़ों failures analyze की हैं।
Character 1: [defensive] पर हमने research की थी! Surveys थे, focus groups थे, सब कुछ जो advisors ने कहा था—हम इतने completely गलत कैसे हो सकते थे लोग क्या चाहते हैं इस बारे में?
43. देखो startup bootcamps में जो नहीं सिखाते वो ये है: लोगों से पूछना कि वो क्या चाहते हैं और actually observe करना कि कौन से problems उन्हें रात को सोने नहीं देते, इनमें ज़मीन-आसमान का फर्क है। [thoughtful pause]
Character 1: [frustrated exhale] तो तुम कह रही हो कि हमारी पूरी methodology ही day one से गलत थी? कि वो सारे positive survey responses basically बेकार थे क्योंकि हम गलत सवाल पूछ रहे थे?
44. [warmly] बेकार नहीं, बस अधूरे—लोगों ने तुम्हें वो बताया जो उन्हें लगा कि तुम सुनना चाहती हो, वो नहीं जिसकी उन्हें actually ज़रूरत थी, क्योंकि जब तुम उन्हें clipboards लेकर एक कमरे में बिठाओगे तो human nature यही है।
Character 1: [quieter] Investors next week pull out कर रहे हैं अगर हम उन्हें pivot strategy नहीं दिखा पाए, और honestly, मुझे तो समझ ही नहीं आ रहा कि इस mess से rebuild कहाँ से शुरू करूं।
45. [leaning forward] अपने target market के बारे में जो भी तुम्हें लगता है कि तुम जानती हो, सब भूल जाओ और तीन दिन बस उन्हें देखो कि वो actually अपनी ज़िंदगी कैसे जीते हैं—कोई सवाल नहीं, कोई pitch नहीं, बस conscious observation।
Character 1: [skeptical] तुम चाहती हो कि मैं basically अपने potential customers को stalk करूं? ये कैसे एक company को बचाएगा जो पैसे खो रही है और जिसके पास exactly दो हफ्ते का runway बचा है?
46. [firmly] इसे ethnographic research कहते हैं।
Character 1: [desperate laugh] हाँ, fancy words ये admit करने के लिए कि हमने कुछ ऐसा बनाया जो किसी ने माँगा ही नहीं था—भगवान, मम्मी को तो मज़े आएंगे जब पता चलेगा कि उनका dropout बेटा ठीक से fail भी नहीं कर सका।
47. [compassionate] तुम्हारी मम्मी ने कल मुझे call किया था actually, ताने देने के लिए नहीं बल्कि पूछने के लिए कि वो कैसे help कर सकती हैं बिना तुम्हें और बुरा feel कराए—वो तुम्हारे try करने पर उतनी proud हैं जितना तुम्हें realize ही नहीं है।
Character 1: [surprised] उन्होंने तुम्हें call किया? Of course, ज़रूर inside scoop चाहिए होगा कि मैंने कितनी बुरी तरह सब कुछ screw up किया है। [sighs heavily]
48. [measured] सुनो, मैं ये काम 15 साल से कर रही हूँ, और जो founders succeed करते हैं वो वो नहीं हैं जो कभी fail नहीं करते—वो हैं जो consciously fail करते हैं, हर lesson को wreckage से निकालते हैं।
Character 1: [softer] तुम्हें सच में लगता है यहाँ कुछ salvageable है? क्योंकि अभी तो मुझे बस अपनी ज़िंदगी के 3 साल और दूसरे लोगों के 2 million dollars धुएं में उड़ते दिख रहे हैं।
49. [encouraging] तुमने जो technology बनाई है वो solid है, team talented है, और सबसे important, अब तुम्हारे पास invaluable data है कि क्या काम नहीं करता—ये actually ज़्यादातर successful launches से ज़्यादा सिखाता है।
Character 1: [growing hopeful] तो जब तुम ethnographic research कहती हो, मतलब literally लोगों के पीछे जाना, उनकी daily routines देखना, वो gaps ढूंढना जो हम miss कर गए क्योंकि हम अपने solution पर ज़्यादा focus कर रहे थे?
50. [energized] Exactly! और मैं तुम्हारी help करूंगी—हम behavioral patterns map कर सकते हैं, genuine friction points identify कर सकते हैं, उनकी choices के पीछे के emotional drivers समझ सकते हैं, सिर्फ वो logical नहीं जो वो surveys में बताते हैं।
Character 1: [determined] ठीक है, तीन दिन observation, फिर क्या? हम उन insights को कैसे कुछ ऐसा बनाएं जिसे present करके investors हमें room से बाहर ना हंसा दें?
51. [confidently] हम customer से backwards तुम्हारी technology तक एक story बनाएंगे, दिखाएंगे कि कैसे एक pivot real, observed pain points को address करता है—investors उन problems के solutions fund करते हैं जिन्हें वो visualize कर सकें, और exactly यही हम उन्हें देंगे।
Character 1: Look, I know you're just trying to do your job, but we've got forty thousand pounds of halibut sitting in what used to be, um, a functioning freezer system, and your welding crew just torched through the main coolant line. [exhales sharply]
52. [defensive] We were following the specs your maintenance team gave us, okay? Nobody said anything about active coolant lines running through that section of the dock structure—I mean, who puts refrigeration pipes inside load-bearing beams anyway?
Character 1: [increasingly urgent] It's a retrofit from the eighties when they expanded the plant, and yeah, it's not ideal, but that's, uh, that's beside the point because right now the temperature is climbing and we're about to lose the entire week's catch.
53. [firmly] Alright, alright, let me think here—my crew's got portable welding rigs and we could probably patch that line in, what, maybe two hours if we really push it? But you'd need to, um, drain the system first.
Character 1: Two hours? Jesus, the fish'll be at room temperature by then, and once the cold chain breaks, that's it, we can't sell to any of our distributors. [pause] This is gonna bankrupt us.
54. [quieter] Wait, hang on, what if we—okay this is crazy but hear me out—what if we bypass the damaged section entirely and run a temporary line over the dock?
Character 1: A temporary line? With what exactly, because last I checked, industrial coolant pipes aren't something you just, [sighs], grab from Home Depot on a Saturday afternoon.
55. [determined] Actually, yeah, we can.
Character 1: [incredulous] Look, I've been processing fish for fifteen years and I've never seen anyone successfully jerry-rig a cooling system with hardware store supplies—it's not just about the pipes, it's the pressure ratings, the insulation, the whole thing.
56. [growing confident] No, listen, I did emergency repairs on refrigerated shipping containers in the Navy for six years before this—we can use flexible metal gas lines with the right adapters, pack them in foam insulation, and it'll hold for at least, uh, seventy-two hours. [exhales] Long enough to save your catch.
Character 1: [hopeful but cautious] You're serious about this? Because if it fails, we're not just losing the fish, we're violating about twelve different health codes and probably getting the whole plant shut down.
57. [steadily] I'm dead serious, and honestly, I feel responsible for this mess even though it wasn't really our fault—those blueprints were wrong. But hey, my crew's here, we've got the tools, and I know exactly what we need.
Character 1: [breathing heavily] Okay, okay, let's do it then, but I'm coming with you to get the supplies because I need to know exactly what we're working with here. [determined] My father built this business from nothing.
58. [reassuring] Your dad sounds like he was a smart guy, building all this, and we're gonna make sure his legacy doesn't melt away today, alright? Let me just grab my truck keys and call my best welder back from lunch.
Character 1: Uh, thank you. Really.
59. Don't thank me yet—we've still got to make this work, and I'm gonna need every person you've got who knows anything about refrigeration systems to help us map out where these bypass lines should run.
Character 1: [energized] I can get you three guys who've been maintaining these systems since before I started, and they know every pipe, every valve, every quirk of this whole setup like it's their own home.
60. [chuckling] Perfect, because we're about to perform emergency surgery on this place, and I'd rather not accidentally cut into something else important while we're at it, you know?
Character 1: [lighter] Yeah, one disaster per day is definitely our limit—although honestly, after we fix this, I'm buying your whole crew dinner, and not just fish and chips either. [small laugh]
61. [warmly] Hey, I'll take you up on that, but first let's save forty thousand pounds of halibut from becoming very expensive cat food, yeah? Time's ticking and that temperature gauge isn't getting any friendlier.
Character 1: वाह, एकदम perfect timing—मैं तूफान का damage देखने आई हूँ और कोई literally मेरे solar panel की पूरी wiring ही नोच रहा है।
62. [defensive] सुनो, मुझे नहीं लगा था कि कोई यहाँ weeks तक वापस आएगा, okay? पूरा district evacuate हो चुका है और आधी buildings तो condemned हैं already।
Character 1: अरे वाह, क्या logic है—चलो जो थोड़े-बहुत sustainable systems hurricane से बच गए थे, उन्हें भी तोड़ डालते हैं क्योंकि, क्या, copper के दाम अच्छे चल रहे हैं इस हफ्ते?
63. तुम्हें लगता है मैं मज़े के लिए ये कर रही हूँ? मेरा apartment पानी में डूबा है, literally पानी में, और FEMA वाले कह रहे हैं relief checks आने में महीनों लगेंगे।

471. The specifications were based on the information I was given by project management, and frankly, welders aren't qualified to evaluate electrical load calculations anyway.

Character 1: Accidents happen when equipment fails randomly, not when an engineer specifies 60-amp breakers for a 120-amp load because he couldn't be bothered to verify the actual machinery specs.

Character 1: That documentation you're hiding behind had the model number wrong, which anyone who actually looked at the equipment would have caught immediately.
476. Field verification wasn't part of my contracted scope, and honestly, if you were so concerned about safety, why didn't you raise these issues before the accident?
Character 1: [seething] Because I trusted that someone with a master's degree and fifteen years of experience would know the difference between a 3-phase and single-phase motor rating.
477. The motor specifications in the database showed single-phase, and without a formal change order indicating otherwise, I had no reason to question it.
Character 1: [flatly] You had no reason.
478. [exasperated] What do you want from me? An apology? An admission of guilt that my lawyers specifically advised against? I followed protocols, documented everything, and the company's insurance covered the damages.

Character 1: Ms. Chen, please sit down, we have some, mmm, rather pressing matters to discuss about your recent partnership deals in Eastern Europe. I believe you've been working with my associates without, uh, without knowing it.

Character 1: [resigned] मेरी engineer का नाम Sarah Kim है, उसे दो assistants चाहिए होंगे, और हमें clean room चाहिए temperature control के साथ 68 से 71 degrees Fahrenheit के बीच।

504. [regretful] I keep seeing their faces. The Hendersons. Standing there in the mud where their barn used to be. [pause] Three generations on that land, and I— I flooded it all away because I pulled the wrong gate. [very sad] One lever. That's all it took. Twenty seconds of not paying attention and their entire wheat crop is gone. Their house, the foundation's cracked. The animals they couldn't get out in time... [sigh] I can't stop thinking about the sound the water made when it hit. Like this, um, like this roar that shouldn't have been there. [angry] God, I'm such an idiot! How do you mess up something you've done a thousand times? [shaky voice] They were so quiet when I tried to apologize. The old man just looked at me and said "mistakes happen" but his eyes were just... empty. [anxious] The company's insurance will cover the damages, they keep telling me that, but that's not— that's not the point. 515. मैं सही थी। [bitter] मैं शुरू से ही सही थी उस jurisdiction के मामले में। छह महीने तक वो लोग कहते रहे कि मैं बेकार में overthink कर रही हूँ, ज़्यादा सतर्क हो रही हूँ, और देखो—judge ने बिल्कुल उसी technicality पर case फेंक दिया। [pause] लेकिन जो बात... अम्म... जो बात मुझे अंदर से खाए जा रही है। सही होने से क्या फ़ायदा जब Mrs. Chen का घर फिर भी चला गया? [frustrated] Bank के वकीलों को पता था। उन्हें पता था कि हमारा case ज़्यादा मज़बूत है तो बस... खींचते रहे matter को। Motion पर motion file करते रहे जब तक उनके पैसे ख़त्म नहीं हो गए। Trial तक पहुँचने से पहले ही पैसे ख़त्म। [regretful] मुझे चाहिए था कि, हम्म, शुरू से ही pro bono के लिए ज़ोर देती। ये आने वाला था, समझना चाहिए था मुझे। लेकिन मैं तो बस legal strategy में सही होने पर इतनी focus थी कि मैंने—मेरा मतलब, क्या फ़ायदा जंग जीतने का अगर तुम्हारा client ही हार जाए? 516. Two years. Two fucking years I've been working toward this and they just... they just sent an email? [bitter] "Due to unforeseen budget constraints" — are you kidding me? [angry] How is this unforeseen when I've been paying tuition for, what, four semesters already? [long pause] I literally rearranged my entire life for this. [upset] Took out loans, quit my job at the clinic because the hours wouldn't work with practicum. My mom thought I was crazy anyway, wanting to work with dead people, but I was so sure, you know? 585. [resigned] 72 घंटे में पूरी city government को relocate करना। [laughs bitterly] Media का तो मेला लग जाएगा, और opposition इसका use करके हमारे पिछले 4 साल की सारी मेहनत बर्बाद कर देगी।
Character 1: [sternly] आपने जो कुछ भी बनाया है, it won't matter if the building collapses with people inside. [pause] मैंने देखा है कि क्या होता है जब warnings को ignore किया जाता है, और मैं वो मौतें अपने conscience पर नहीं ले सकती।
586. आप मुझसे कह रही हैं कि मैं mayor को बताऊं कि उनकी पूरी administration को city hall छोड़नी होगी। [very quietly] इससे careers खत्म हो जाएंगे, मेरा भी, and probably trigger a federal investigation into municipal negligence.
Character 1: [resolutely] मैं request नहीं कर रही, Ms. Rodriguez। [clears throat] Condemnation notice already state के साथ file हो चुका है, और copies अभी हर department head को deliver की जा रही हैं।
587. [defeated] भगवान हमारी मदद करे।
Character 1: [warmly] अगर मदद चाहिए तो, I can connect you with emergency relocation specialists जिन्होंने दूसरी municipalities में similar situations handle की हैं। [pause] ये उतनी बड़ी disaster नहीं बननी चाहिए जितना आप सोच रही हैं।
588. [suspiciously] आप help क्यों करेंगी?
Character 1: क्योंकि आप जो सोच रही होंगी उसके विपरीत, I don't enjoy destroying careers or creating chaos. [sincerely] मैं बस चाहती हूँ कि लोग दिन के अंत में safely अपने परिवार के पास जाएं, including your daughter.
589. [reluctantly] ठीक है, मुझे उन specialists की contact information भेज दीजिए। [sighs heavily] मैं एक घंटे में department heads की emergency meeting बुलाऊंगी, हालांकि honestly मुझे नहीं पता कि मैं कैसे explain करूंगी कि हम सालों से एक death trap में काम कर रहे थे without knowing it. [pause] या शायद हमें पता था और हमने बस नज़रअंदाज़ करना चुना।
Character 1: [shaky voice] You said on the phone that you found something underneath the paint layers of Emma's self-portrait, something she deliberately hid before she— [pause] I've been standing outside this lab for twenty minutes trying to work up the courage to come in.
590. [hesitantly] The infrared spectroscopy revealed extensive underpainting, words and images she covered with thick layers of oils. [quietly] I've been doing this work for fifteen years, and I've never seen someone use a canvas like a diary the way your sister did.
Character 1: [anxious] Emma always said that painting was the only time she felt real, like her actual self could finally breathe. [sighs] We were identical twins, but I never understood what she meant until now.
591. [carefully] The messages progress chronologically from the bottom layers upward, starting about six months before her death. [clearing throat] Some of them mention you specifically, things she wanted to say but couldn't.
Character 1: [crying while speaking] What kind of things? [very quietly] I keep thinking if I'd just paid more attention, if I hadn't been so wrapped up in my own life, maybe I would have seen the signs.
592. She wrote 'My twin lives in daylight while I drown in paint fumes and shadows' across the entire bottom layer. [pause] There's also a sketch of two girls holding hands that she covered with black paint.
Character 1: We used to hold hands everywhere as kids, even in high school until people started making fun of us. [bitter] I was the one who pulled away first, said we needed to grow up and be individuals.
593. [empathetically] The chemical analysis shows she returned to this painting repeatedly, adding layers whenever she was struggling. [softly] The final layer, applied just days before, contains a single word repeated seventeen times.
Character 1: [barely audible] What word? [shaky voice] Please, I need to know everything she couldn't tell me when she was alive, even if it destroys me.
594. [very quietly] 'Sister' written over and over in cadmium red, the most expensive pigment she owned. [sighs] She mixed it with tears, we can tell from the salt crystals that formed as it dried.
Character 1: [monotone] She called me three times that last week, but I was at a conference in Seattle and kept sending her to voicemail. [laughs bitterly] I texted her that we'd catch up when I got back.
595. [gently] There's more.
Character 1: [desperate] Every therapist keeps telling me survivor's guilt is normal for twins, that I couldn't have known, but they didn't see her painting becoming darker month by month. [exhales] I saw everything and did nothing.
596. [pause] Should I continue?
Character 1: [firmly] Yes, tell me all of it. [crying while speaking] I owe her that much at least, to witness what she needed me to see when it mattered.
597. [slowly] Beneath the repeated 'sister' text, in the deepest layer we could access without damaging the canvas, she painted both your faces but gave you her eyes and herself yours. [very quietly] The inscription reads 'We were supposed to share everything, even this.'
Character 1: [gasping] Oh god, she thought about taking me with her? [shaky voice] Is that what she meant? That we should have died together?
598. [carefully] I think she meant the pain, that she wanted to share the pain with you but couldn't figure out how. [sighs] The technical notes indicate she spent over a hundred hours just on those exchanged eyes.
Character 1: [whispering] Can I touch it? [louder] The painting, I mean, just once where her hands were, where she pressed her feelings into the canvas?
599. [warmly] Normally I'd say absolutely not, but in this case, yes. [softly] Your sister embedded so much of herself in these layers that perhaps she'd want you to feel what she couldn't say. [pause] Here, put on these gloves first.
Character 1: [surprised] Margaret, what are you doing with all these boxes? [pause] I just got home from the press conference, और तुम अपना office ऐसे pack कर रही हो जैसे कल ही जा रही हो।
600. [bitter] Four point two billion dollars, यही कह रहे हैं news में। [quietly] Fifteen years I've managed this house, और मुझे पता चला कि तुमने company बेच दी, वो भी TV पे एक reporter से।
Character 1: [apologetic] I wanted to tell you first, सच में बताना चाहती थी, लेकिन lawyers ने NDAs sign करवाए थे, announcement public होने तक। [sighs] Even my own mother didn't know, एक घंटे पहले तक।
601. [hurt] Your mother doesn't live in your guest house, तुम्हारा schedule manage नहीं करती, नहीं जानती कि तुम कब खाना छोड़ देती हो quarterly reports के stress में। [voice breaking] I thought I'd earned more, मुझे लगा था मैं इतनी तो हकदार हूँ कि अजनबियों के साथ ना सुनूं।
Character 1: [empathetically] You're right, Margaret, तुम बेहतर deserve करती थी। [pause] The deal happened so fast, और मैं पिछले 72 घंटे से boardrooms में फंसी थी, सबके interests protect करने की कोशिश में, तुम्हारे भी।
602. Mine? [sarcastically] कैसे exactly protect कर रही थी मेरे interests, जब new owners के पास शायद अपना staff already ready होगा?
Character 1: [firmly] Because I made your continued employment a condition of the sale. [warmly] पूरी salary, benefits, और five साल का contract अगर तुम चाहो, plus एक bonus जिससे तुम अपना घर खरीद सको।
603. [shocked] Wait, क्या कहा तुमने?
Character 1: [gratefully] You kept me human, जब बाकी सब को सिर्फ dollar signs और stock options दिखते थे। [voice breaking] You made sure I ate real food, मेरी बहन का birthday याद रखा, यहां तक कि मेरे कुत्ते को vet के पास ले गईं जब मैं Shanghai में फंसी थी।
604. [softly] You wrote my employment into a four billion dollar deal? [exhales] ये तो बहुत complicated रहा होगा, इतने सारे lawyers और executives हर छोटी बात पे argue कर रहे होंगे।
Character 1: [confidently] They wanted to argue about it, फिर मैंने उन्हें याद दिलाया कि तुम्हारे बिना मेरी life manage करने वाला कोई नहीं था, मैं कभी कुछ build ही नहीं कर पाती जो खरीदने लायक होता। [chuckles] उनके चेहरे देखने लायक थे।
605. [warmly] I'm sorry for packing without talking to you first. [sighs] मुझे लगा इतने पैसे के साथ, तुम fresh start चाहोगी, शायद किसी younger को hire करोगी जो तुम्हारे सारे tech gadgets बेहतर समझती हो।
Character 1: [laughing] Margaret, तुम ही एक हो जो मेरे smart home को actually ठीक से चला सकती हो। [pause] Remember when those venture capitalists came for dinner, और तुमने automated blinds को bobby pin से ठीक किया था?
606. [chuckling] They kept calling it a 'revolutionary hack', पूछ रहे थे कि क्या तुमने मुझे coding सिखाई है। [warmly] मैंने नहीं बताया कि ये trick मैंने 1987 में अपनी दादी की sewing machine ठीक करते हुए सीखी थी।
Character 1: [sincerely] Look, I know I handled this badly, लेकिन एक important बात समझनी होगी। [slowly] You're not just staff to me, तुम family हो, और family साथ रहती है ऐसे transitions में।

Character 1: [very sincerely] I don't want anyone else, मुझे कोई और नहीं चाहिए।
608. [relieved] Then I suppose I should unpack these boxes, और सोचना शुरू करूं कि एक billionaire का household कैसे manage करना है। [pause] Will you at least try to give me a heads up, अगली life-changing announcement से पहले?
Character 1: [grateful] I promise, पक्का वादा।
609. [warmly] Good, क्योंकि तुम्हारा dinner ठंडा हो रहा है और कल वो charity gala है जो तुम भूल गई हो। [chuckles] Billions of dollars don't change the fact, तुम अभी भी अपना calendar याद नहीं रख सकती।
Character 1: [firmly] डॉक्टर हैरिसन।
610. मिस चेन, कृपया बैठिए। [formally] मैं समझती हूं कि आपने ये मीटिंग मांगी थी अपनी बेटी के केस के बारे में बात करने के लिए, though I should mention that my determination was based on established medical criteria.
Character 1: [controlled] मैं हर रोज़ Medicaid applications process करती हूं, परिवारों को देखती हूं जो coverage के लिए भीख मांगते हैं जबकि उनके बच्चे तड़प रहे होते हैं। [bitter] कभी नहीं सोचा था कि मैं इस तरफ बैठूंगी, arguing why my daughter deserves to live.
611. [confidently] जो ablation procedure आपकी बेटी को चाहिए वो elective है उसकी current state में। [stern] उसके arrhythmia episodes चिंताजनक हैं ज़रूर, लेकिन medication से manage हो सकते हैं for several more years before surgical intervention becomes necessary.
Character 1: [frustrated] कई साल और? [loudly] वो स्कूल में दो बार गिर चुकी है पिछले महीने, soccer नहीं खेल पा रही, रातों को डर के मारे जागती रहती है कि her heart will just stop beating while she sleeps.
612. [empathetically] मैं समझती हूं ये आप दोनों के लिए कितना डरावना है, but the medical guidelines are clear about intervention thresholds. [pause] हमें sustained ventricular tachycardia देखनी होगी 200 beats per minute से ऊपर, तभी surgery indicated होगी।
Character 1: पता है क्या ironic है? [exhales] कल मुझे एक दादी की diabetes supplies के लिए coverage deny करनी पड़ी क्योंकि वो income limit से 12 डॉलर ऊपर थीं, और यहां मैं आपसे विनती कर रही हूं कि अपना decision reconsider करिए।
613. [defensively] ये पैसे या insurance bureaucracy के बारे में नहीं है मिस चेन। [firmly] ये medical necessity के बारे में है, और एक 14 साल की बच्ची को unnecessary surgical risks से बचाने के बारे में है whose condition might stabilize with proper medication management.
Character 1: [angrily] Might stabilize? [trembling] आप मेरी बेटी की ज़िंदगी से जुआ खेल रही हैं क्योंकि statistics कहते हैं कि she probably won't die in the next few years, बस हर दिन तड़पती रहेगी।
614. [quietly] मेरी भी एक बेटी है, 16 साल की, violin बजाती है। [sighs] लेकिन medical decisions emotion पर based नहीं हो सकते, they have to follow evidence-based protocols that protect patients from unnecessary procedures.
Character 1: [passionately] Evidence-based protocols जो उन लोगों ने लिखे हैं जिन्होंने कभी अपने बच्चे को सांस के लिए तड़पते नहीं देखा, जो पूछते हैं कि क्या वो मर रही है। [voice breaking] हर guideline जो आप quote करती हैं, that's another night I don't sleep.

Character 1: [shocked] आप मुझसे कह रही हैं कि मैं इंतज़ार करूं कि मेरी बेटी को तीन और cardiac events हों? [bitter laugh] उम्मीद करूं कि वो इतनी बीमार हो जाए कि qualify करे लेकिन इतनी नहीं कि हम उसे खो दें?
616. [regretful] मैं जानती हूं ये कैसा सुनाई दे रहा है, but it's the only way within the system to justify the surgery sooner. [quietly] जब तक आप privately procedure afford नहीं कर सकतीं, जो करीब 2 लाख डॉलर होगा।
Character 1: 2 लाख डॉलर। [laughs bitterly] मैं साल में 38 हज़ार कमाती हूं दूसरों की मदद करते हुए इस टूटे सिस्टम में, उन्हें बताती हूं कि उम्मीद है अगर वो सही forms भर दें।

Character 1: [surprised] आप उसी system को game करने में हमारी मदद कर रही हैं जिसे आपने अभी 10 मिनट defend किया? [confused] आप अपनी standing क्यों risk करेंगी insurance company के साथ हमारे लिए?
618. [warmly] क्योंकि मैं जानती हूं कि medically necessary और humanly necessary में क्या फर्क है। [sighs] और क्योंकि मैं भी वहां रही हूं जहां आप हैं, watching my own child suffer while bureaucracy moved at glacial speed.
Character 1: [relieved] शुक्रिया। [voice shaking] मैं हफ्तों से आप पर इतनी गुस्सा थी, आपका denial letter बार-बार पढ़ती रही, और यहां आप सच में हमारी मदद करने की कोशिश कर रही हैं।
619. [gently] Emma को कल 3 बजे लेकर आइए, हम full workup करेंगे और case build करना शुरू करेंगे। [determined] आपकी system की knowledge और मेरे medical documentation के साथ, we'll get your daughter the surgery she needs.
